Layers of Mujtahid and the Role of Qawa'id
Defining the layers of mujtahid and necessity of qawa'id

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the five categories of mujtahids (independent and four affiliated types) and explain the necessity of qawa'id for ijtihad.

Core Idea
Ijtihad has layers; affiliated mujtahids work within madhhab principles, and all ijtihad requires a framework of qawa'id.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text outlines the hierarchical classification of mujtahids, from fully independent to mere transmitter, and underscores that every mujtahid must operate with a system of legal rules (qawa'id). Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for assessing the authority of legal opinions and the proper methodology of ijtihad within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
The passage divides mujtahids into 'mustaqill' (independent) and 'muntasib' (affiliated). Note the conditions for the independent mujtahid, which have been absent for long periods.
The independent mujtahid requires complete mastery of all tools of ijtihad.
2
List the four types of affiliated mujtahid
The affiliated mujtahid is subdivided into four ranks: (1) does not imitate imam in proof; (2) restricted mujtahid within madhhab (ashab al-wujuh); (3) below ashab al-wujuh but still a faqih; (4) transmitter weak in proof. Recognize the characteristics of each.
The second type describes those who can derive rulings using the imam's principles but lack independent tools like deep grammar/hadith knowledge.
3
Understand the critique and accepted classification
The author critiques a group that misapplied the classification and claims superiority. The accepted Hanafi view, endorsed by al-Laknawi and al-Kawthari, is the four-category division above.
The critique warns against reckless claims of ijtihad beyond one's level.
4
Grasp the necessity of qawa'id
The passage argues that ijtihad, especially for affiliated mujtahids, must be based on a set of rules (qawa'id) derived from the imam's principles. These rules allow efficient derivation for new cases.
Qawa'id are not a replacement for evidence but a stage-based tool reflecting the madhhab's methodology.
5
Apply the classification
Given a description of a scholar, identify which category he falls into based on his knowledge and method. This helps in evaluating the authority of his fatwas.
The mufta bihi ruling is that the affiliated mujtahid's fatwa is valid within his scope.

Source Text

للنووي (1) : «إنّ المجتهد : ا . إما مجتهد مستقل : ومن شروطه فقه النفس، وسلامة الذهن، ورياضة الفكر، وصحة التصرف والاستنباط، والتيقظ، ومعرفة الأدلة وآلاتها المذكورة في الأصول وشروطها، والاقتباس منها مع الدراية والارتياض في استعمالها، ومع الفقه والضبط لأمهات مسائله ، وهذا عُدِمَ من أزمنة طويلة.
٢. وإما منتسب : وهو أربعة أقسام :
أحدها: أن لا يقلد إمامه في المذهب والدليل ؛ لاتصافه بصفة المستقل، وإنما ينسب إليه لسلوك طريقه في الاجتهاد.
وثانيها : أن يكون مجتهداً مقيداً في المذهب، مستقلاً بتقرير أصوله بالدليل، غير أنه لا يتجاوز في أدلة أصول إمامه وقواعده، وشرطه كونه عالماً بالفقه وأصوله وأدلة الأحكام تفصيلاً، وكونه بصيرا بمسالك الأقيسة والمعاني، تام الارتياض في التخريج والاستنباط ؛ لقياس غير المنصوص عليه ؛ لعلمه بأصول إمامه، ولا يعرى عن تقليد له ، لإخلاله ببعض أدوات المستقل ؛ كالنحو والحديث ، وهذه صفة أصحابنا أصحاب الوجوه.
وثالثها : أن لا يبلغ رتبة الوجوه، لكنّه فقية حافظ مذهب إمامه، قائم بتقرير أدلته ، يصور ويحرِّرُ ويقررُ ويمهد ويزيفُ ويرجّح، وهذه صفة كثير من المتأخرين إلى أواخر المئة الرابعة الذين رتبوا المذهب وحرّروا (۳).
فغلطوا في ذلك ، ثم أكثروا في الكلام من نحو هذه الخرافات والمجازفات، وسولت له نفسه أنه أبرز أدلة خفيت عليهم، وأن تقليده أو تقليد شيخه التابع له في الحل أولى من تقليدهم، فلعظيم ضرر . هذه الحادثة وسوء صنيع وطوية هذا المجازف جردت صارم العزم وباتر التنقيب والفحص والفهم، وأوريت زند الفكر حمية لأئمتنا غيوث الهدى ومصابيح الدجى...... (۱) هو شارح «صحیح مسلم» يحيى بن شرف النووي المتوفى سنة (٦٧٧) أو سنة (٦٧٦). منه رحمه الله.
(۲) ومصدر الاجتهاد الوحيد عند هذه الطبقة كما فصلته في المدخل ( ص ٢٢٣) هو : «ما نقل إليهم من كلام أئمة المذهب الذين يقلدون أهله»، قال الإمام النووي الشافعي في «المجموع»(١ : ٧٦) ، والإمام المرداوي الحنبلي (ت ٨٨٥هـ) في «الإنصاف» (١٢ : ٢٦٠): «يتخذ نـصـوص إمـامـه أصولا يستنبط منها كفعل المستقل بنصوص الشرع». وإن اعترض عليهم بأن أقوال الأئمة غير معصومة فكيف تنزل منزلة الوحيين المعصومين ؛ لأن ما روي عن الإمام صاحب المذهب ليس قرآناً ، ولا أحاديث صحيحة، فكيف تستنبط الأحكام منه؟ فإنه يجاب بما يلي : إنه كلام أئمة مجتهدين عالمين بقواعد الشريعة والعربية، مبينين للأحكام الشرعية، فمدلول
ورابعها : أن يقوم بحفظ المذهب ونقله، وفهم مشكله، ولكنه ضعيف في تقرير دليله، وتحرير أقيسته، فهذا يعتبر نقله وفتواه فيما يحكيه من مسطورات مذهبه». انتهى ملخصاً (۲).
كلامهم حجة على من قلدهم، منطوقاً كان أو مفهوماً صريحاً كان أو إشارة، فكلامهم بالنسبة له كالقرآن والحديث بالنسبة لجميع المجتهدين. وله فضل عظيم لا يستطيع أحد إنكاره ، وهو أنه فتح باباً واسعاً لتطور الفقه ومسايرته لأحداث الحياة» ينظر: «الموسوعة الفقهية المصرية» (۱ : ٢٠).
٦
٢. إنه لا يكون اجتهاد مجتهد إلا بأن يكون له قواعد يحتكم إليها في استخراج الأحكام الفقهية ، سواء كان هو واضعها أو قلّد فيها غيره ؛ لأن استنباط الأحكام الفقهية من الكتاب والسنة يحتاج إلى أصول وقواعد، فمثلاً : إذا تعارضت الأحاديث في الدلالة على حكم من الأحكام يستطيع بالقواعد التي يمشي عليها أن يستخرجه. إذا تقرر هذا فإنه يمكن القول بأن كلام المجتهد في المسائل الفقهية هو تطبيق لقواعده وأصوله التي اعتمدها في استخراج الأحكام، ففي اعتماد حكمه قطع لمرحلة طويلة وصعبة جدا من استنباط للحكم من الأدلة التفصيلية. فالأمـر أمـر مـرحـلـية وتدرج، وليس إهمالاً وتركاً للأدلة الشرعية ؛ لأن أحكام المجتهد مأخوذة من الأدلة، فهي تمثلها، ولكنها قطعت مرحلة للمجتهد في المذهب لاستخراج الأحكام التي لم يبينها المجتهد.
وتأكيد هذا ما يلاحظ في القواعد الفقهية التي استخرجت من مجموعة الأحكام الفقهية المتناثرة المتفقة فيما بينهما، ومن ثم يمكن الاعتماد على القاعدة في معرفة الأحكام غير المبينة كما هو معلوم. ينظر : «المنهج الفقهي للإمام اللكنوي»(ص١٤٨ - ١٤٩).
(۱) هذا التقسيم لطبقات المجتهدين ارتضاه الإمام اللكنوي بعد أن نقض التقسيم السابق، وكذلك قبله الإمام الكوثري في حسن التقاضي» (ص (٢٤) ، وهو الأحرى بالقبول، والله أعلم. (۲) من المجموع شرح المهذب»(۱ : ۷۷).
According to al-Nawawi (1): 'Indeed, the mujtahid: either an independent mujtahid, and among its conditions are: deep understanding, soundness of mind, practice of thought, correctness of deduction and inference, vigilance, knowledge of the evidences and their tools mentioned in usul and their conditions, and extracting from them with expertise and practice in their use, and knowledge and mastery of the major issues of his discipline. This has been absent for long periods. 2. Or affiliated, and it is four categories: First: that he does not follow his imam in madhhab or proof, because he is characterized by the quality of the independent, but he is attributed to him because he pursues his method in ijtihad. Second: that he is a restricted mujtahid within the madhhab, independent in establishing its principles with proof, but he does not go beyond the proofs and principles of his imam. Its condition is that he be knowledgeable in fiqh, its principles, and detailed proofs of rulings, and be insightful in the methods of analogy and meanings, fully practiced in deduction and inference for analogizing what is not explicitly stated, due to his knowledge of his imam's principles, and he is not free from following him, because he lacks some tools of the independent, such as grammar and hadith. This is the description of our companions, the people of wajh. Third: that he does not reach the rank of the people of wajh, but he is a faqih who preserves his imam's madhhab, undertakes to establish its proofs, conceptualizes, edits, decides, lays foundations, refutes, and prefers. This is the description of many from the later scholars up to the end of the fourth century who arranged and edited the madhhab (3). So they erred in that, then they spoke much of similar nonsense and reckless statements, and his soul tempted him that he produced proofs that were hidden from them, and that his taqlid or the taqlid of his shaykh who follows him in the solution is more deserving than their taqlid. Due to the great harm of this incident and the evil deed and intention of this reckless person, I unsheathed the sword of determination and the decisive blade of investigation, examination, and understanding, and I struck the flint of thought with zeal for our imams, the rain clouds of guidance and the lamps of darkness... (1) He is the commentator of Sahih Muslim, Yahya ibn Sharaf al-Nawawi, who died in 677 or 676 AH. May Allah have mercy on him. (2) The only source of ijtihad for this category, as I detailed in the introduction (p. 223), is: 'What is transmitted to them from the words of the imams of the madhhab whom they follow.' Imam al-Nawawi al-Shafi'i said in al-Majmu' (1:76) and Imam al-Mardawi al-Hanbali in al-Insaf (12:260): 'He takes the texts of his imam as principles from which he deduces, like the independent does with the texts of the Shari'ah.' And if it is objected that the sayings of the imams are not infallible, so how can they be placed in the position of the two infallible revelations? Because what is reported from the imam of the madhhab is not Quran nor authentic hadiths. So how can rulings be derived from it? The answer is: They are words of mujtahid imams, knowledgeable in the principles of Shari'ah and Arabic, clarifying the legal rulings. So their meaning is evidence for those who follow them, explicitly or implicitly, clearly or by indication. Their words are for him like the Quran and Hadith are for all mujtahids. And they have a great virtue that no one can deny, namely that they opened a wide door for the development of fiqh and its adaptation to the events of life. See: al-Mawsu'ah al-Fiqhiyyah al-Misriyyah (1:20). 2. A mujtahid's ijtihad can only be with rules to which he refers in extracting legal rulings, whether he formulated them himself or followed someone else. Because deriving fiqh rulings from the Book and Sunnah requires principles and rules. For example, if hadiths conflict in indicating a ruling, he can derive it with the rules he follows. If this is established, it can be said that the mujtahid's words in fiqh issues are the application of his rules and principles that he relied upon in extracting rulings. So by adopting his ruling, a long and very difficult stage of deriving the ruling from detailed evidences is cut short. The matter is one of stages and gradualism, not neglect or abandonment of legal evidences. Because the rulings of the mujtahid are taken from the evidences, so they represent them, but they have cut a stage for the mujtahid in the madhhab to extract rulings that the mujtahid did not clarify. Confirming this is what is observed in the legal rules extracted from a collection of scattered fiqh rulings that agree with each other. Then one can rely on the rule to know unclear rulings, as is known. See: al-Manhaj al-Fiqhi li'l-Imam al-Laknawi (pp. 148-149). (1) This classification of the layers of mujtahids was accepted by Imam al-Laknawi after he refuted the previous classification, and likewise before him Imam al-Kawthari in Hasan al-Taqadi' (p. 24). It is more worthy of acceptance, and Allah knows best. (2) From al-Majmu' Sharh al-Muhadhdhab (1:77).
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classificatory exposition of the layers of mujtahids within the Hanafi school. The author begins by citing Imam al-Nawawi's classification of mujtahids into independent and affiliated, with the affiliated divided into four categories. The first is the mujtahid who does not imitate his imam in proofs. The second is the restricted mujtahid within the madhhab who establishes its principles with proof but does not go beyond his imam's foundational proofs; this describes 'ashab al-wujuh'. The third is below this level but still a faqih who preserves and transmits the madhhab. The fourth is the transmitter who is weak in proof. The author then critiques a group that made errors in this classification, before presenting the accepted Hanafi view as endorsed by al-Laknawi and al-Kawthari. The second part argues that a mujtahid must have a set of rules (qawa'id) to base his ijtihad upon, whether he formulated them himself or adopted them. This is because deriving rulings from the primary sources requires methodological principles, and the mujtahid's rulings are applications of those principles. The passage emphasizes that this is not a departure from evidence but a stage-based system that allows for the development of fiqh and the extraction of rulings for new cases. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each category briefly and highlighting the Hanafi acceptance of the classification by al-Laknawi.

Key Terms
مجتهد مستقل (mujtahid mustaqill): A fully independent mujtahid who possesses all tools of ijtihad and does not follow any imam; he derives rulings directly from the primary sources.
مجتهد منتسب (mujtahid muntasib): A mujtahid who follows the methodology of a particular imam but may have varying degrees of independence; he is attributed to the madhhab.
أصحاب الوجوه (ashab al-wujuh): Scholars within the Hanafi school who were capable of deriving rulings based on the principles of the madhhab but lacked some tools of the independent mujtahid.
قواعد فقهية (qawa'id fiqhiyya): General legal rules derived from multiple fiqh cases that help in deriving rulings for new situations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following describes the second category of affiliated mujtahid (mujtahid muntasib)?
A) He does not follow his imam in evidence but pursues his method.
B) He is a restricted mujtahid within the madhhab, independent in establishing its principles, but does not go beyond his imam's proofs.
C) He preserves the madhhab and transmits it but is weak in establishing proofs.
D) He is fully independent and derives rulings directly from Quran and Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes multiple levels of ijtihad, with the affiliated mujtahid operating within the madhhab's framework using qawa'id.

Three Layers of Hanafi Texts: Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, Fatawa
Classification of Hanafi legal sources into three hierarchical layers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three layers of Hanafi texts (Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, Fatawa) and explain their hierarchical authority.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is the backbone; Nawadir and Fatawa are secondary layers, with Fatawa being the least authoritative.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah provides a clear classification of Hanafi legal sources. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for any student of Hanafi fiqh, as it determines which rulings carry more weight. The author distinguishes between the well-known transmitted books (Zahir al-Riwayah), rare transmissions (Nawadir), and later fatwas derived for novel cases (Fatawa/Waqi'at).

Guided Path
1
Identify the first layer
The Zahir al-Riwayah are the six core books of Imam Muhammad, transmitted through reliable chains. These form the strongest basis for rulings.
These are considered the most authoritative within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the second layer
The Nawadir include books like al-Mujarrad and the Amali, and scattered narrations from other early Hanafis. They are less authoritative due to weaker transmission.
Some Nawadir contain rulings that contradict the principles of the school.
3
Identify the third layer
The Fatawa (Waqi'at) are rulings derived by later scholars for new cases not covered in earlier texts. They are the weakest layer.
The first collection was al-Nawazil by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi.
4
Understand the historical development
Later works often mixed these layers, but some, like al-Muhit by al-Sarakhsi, kept them separate. This shows the evolution of Hanafi legal literature.
Refer to the passage for the list of early compilers.

Source Text

والهارونيات (۱) ، وإنما سمّي غير ظاهر الرواية ؛ لأنها لم تشتهر عن محمد ده ولم ترو عنه بطرق كطرق الكتب الأول.
٢. وإما في كتب غير محمد ، كـ«المجرد» للحسن بن زياد، ومنها كتب «الأمالي». والإملاء : أن يقعد العالم وحوله تلامذة بالمحابر والقراطيس، فيتكلم العالم بما فتح الله عليه من العلم، وتكتب التلامذة ما تكلّم مجلساً مجلساً، ثم يجمعون ما كتبوا، فيصير كتاباً، وسمي بالأمالي، وكان هذا عادة أصحابنا المتقدمين.
٣. ومنها : الروايات المتفرّقة : كرواية ابن سماعة الله وغيره من أصحاب محمد الا الله ، وغيره من مسائل مخالفة للأصول، فإنّها غير ظاهر الرواية، وتعد من النوادر : کنوادر ابن سماعة ) ، ونوادر هشام ، و نوادر ابن رستم
الطبقة الثالثة : الفتاوى : وتسمى الواقعات وهي مسائل استنبطها المتأخرون من أصحاب محمد الله ، وأصحاب أصحاب محمد الله فمن بعدهم في الواقعات التي لم توجد فيها رواية عن الأئمة الثلاثة، وأوّل كتاب جُمِعَ فيه مما عُلِمَ «النوازل» ألفَه الفقيه أبو الليث نصر بن محمد بن إبراهيم السَّمَرْقَنْدِي، المعروف بإمام الهدى، وجمع فيه فتاوى المتأخرين المجتهدين من مشايخه، وشيوخ مشايخه كمحمّد بن مقاتل الرازي، ومحمد بن سلمة (١) ، ونصير بن يحيى (٢)، وذكر فيها اختياراته أيضاً، وهو أصل الواقعات
ثم جمع المشايخ فيه كتباً : كـ«مجموع النوازل والواقعات» للنَّاطِفِي(۳) والصدر الشهيد وغيره.
ثمَّ جمع من بعدهم من المشايخ هذه الطبقات في فتاواهم مختلطة غير ممتازة، كما في «جامع قاضي خان»، و«الخلاصة»، وغيرهما من كتب الفتاوى ، وقد ميّز بعضُهم كما في «المحيط» لرضي الدين السِّرَخْسِي (٥) فإنه بدأ بمسائل الأصول أولاً ، ثم النوادر ثم الفتاوى. انتهى كلامه(٦).
وقد ذكرتُ بعض ما يتعلّق بهذا البحث في «مقدمة الهداية»، وفي «النافع الكبير لمن يطالع الجامع الصغير)، فليرجع إليهما.
And the Haruniyyat (1), and it is called non-Zahir al-Riwayah because they were not well-known from Muhammad and were not narrated from him through paths like the paths of the first books.
2. Or in books other than Muhammad, such as 'Al-Mujarrad' by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and among them are the books of 'Al-Amalī'. And 'Imlā' is that a scholar sits with students around him with inkwells and papers, then the scholar speaks of what God has opened for him of knowledge, and the students write down what he says session by session, then they collect what they wrote, and it becomes a book, and it is called 'Al-Amalī', and this was the habit of our early companions.
3. And among them: the scattered narrations: such as the narration of Ibn Samā'ah and others from the companions of Muhammad, and other issues contradicting the principles, for they are non-Zahir al-Riwayah, and are counted among the Nawādir: like Nawādir Ibn Samā'ah, and Nawādir Hishām, and Nawādir Ibn Rustam.
The third layer: Al-Fatāwā: also called Al-Wāqi'āt, which are issues deduced by later scholars from the companions of Muhammad and the companions of the companions of Muhammad and those after them, concerning incidents for which no narration from the three Imams existed. The first book compiled in this regard known is 'Al-Nawāzil' authored by the jurist Abu al-Layth Nasr ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Samarqandī, known as Imām al-Hudā. He collected in it the fatāwā of later mujtahid scholars among his teachers and their teachers, such as Muhammad ibn Muqātil al-Rāzī, Muhammad ibn Salamah (1), and Nasīr ibn Yahyā (2), and he also mentioned his own selections. It is the origin of the Wāqi'āt.
Then the scholars compiled books in it: such as 'Majmū' al-Nawāzil wa al-Wāqi'āt' by al-Nāṭifī (3) and al-Sadr al-Shahīd and others.
Then later scholars collected these layers in their fatāwā mixed indistinguishably, as in 'Jāmi' Qāḍī Khān' and 'Al-Khulāṣah' and other books of fatāwā. Some distinguished them, as in 'Al-Muḥīṭ' by Raḍī al-Dīn al-Sarakhsī (5), for he began with issues of the principles first, then the Nawādir, then the Fatāwā. His statement ends (6).
I have mentioned some of what pertains to this discussion in 'Muqaddimat al-Hidāyah' and in 'Al-Nāfi' al-Kabīr li man yuṭāli' al-Jāmi' al-Ṣaghīr', so refer to them.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a methodological introduction from the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'āyah', explaining the three layers of Hanafi legal texts. The author first distinguishes between the well-known transmitted books (Zahir al-Riwayah) from Imam Muhammad's six core works, and other transmissions (Nawadir) which are less reliable because they were not narrated through the same rigorous paths. He then describes the second layer: books not by Muhammad but by other early Hanafis, such as 'Al-Mujarrad' by Hasan ibn Ziyad, and the 'Amali' books (dictations). The third and lowest layer is the Fatāwā (also called Wāqi'āt), which are rulings derived by later scholars for cases not explicitly found in the earlier sources. The first such collection was 'Al-Nawāzil' by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandī. Later compilations mixed these layers, but some works like 'Al-Muḥīṭ' by al-Sarakhsī separated them. The author concludes by referring to his other works for more details.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The well-known transmitted books from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, narrated through reliable chains, forming the core of the Hanafi madhhab.
نوادر (Nawādir): Rare or less-known transmissions from early Hanafi authorities, not part of the six core books, often containing rulings that differ from the principles (uṣūl).
فتاوى (Fatāwā): Rulings deduced by later Hanafi scholars for new cases not found in earlier transmitted texts; also called Wāqi'āt.
واقعات (Wāqi'āt): Incidents or cases for which no explicit ruling is found in the early texts; later scholars derived rulings for them, forming the third layer.
أمالي (Amālī): Books compiled from a scholar's dictation to his students over multiple sittings; a common early method of composing Hanafi texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the correct order of authority for Hanafi texts according to this passage?
A) Fatawa, Nawadir, Zahir al-Riwayah
B) Nawadir, Fatawa, Zahir al-Riwayah
C) Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, Fatawa
D) All are equal in authority

Key Takeaway
Hanafi legal sources are ranked: Zahir al-Riwayah (core), then Nawadir (rare transmissions), then Fatawa (later deductions).

The Authority of Mutūn: General but Not Universal
Clarifying the authority of Hanafi core texts (mutun) as generally but not absolutely representing original madhhab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the authority of Hanafi mutun as generally transmitting the original madhhab but potentially including later derivations, and identify implications for fiqh study.

Core Idea
Mutun are authoritative but not infallible; they may contain later ijtihad and preferred views of the Sahibayn.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary clarifies a common misconception about the core texts (mutun). While they are the primary sources for transmitting the original madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions, their authority is general, not absolute. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly interpreting rulings found in texts like al-Mukhtār and al-Kanz, and for recognizing which statements originate from the founding imams versus later scholarly development.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two claims about mutun
The author refers to two common beliefs: (1) mutun transmit only original madhhab and Zāhir al-Riwāyah, and (2) they transmit only the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. Recognize these as the starting point.
These claims are widely assumed by students.
2
Understand the author's correction
The author states that these rules are 'ghālibī lā kullī' — general, not universal. This means they are tendencies with exceptions.
The terms ghālibī and kullī are key technical concepts in usul.
3
Analyze the first exception: al-ʿashr fī al-ʿashr
The example of 'ten in ten' regarding the impurity of a basin is a later determination by later scholars, not found in the original madhhab. This shows mutun may include rulings outside Zāhir al-Riwāyah.
We don't need to know the details of that fiqh issue now; focus on the methodological point.
4
Analyze the second exception: sujūd with forehead and nose
The ruling that prostration requires both the forehead and the nose is the view of the two companions (Sahibayn). The mutun mention it when it is preponderant, even though it differs from Abu Hanifa's view.
This shows mutun are not limited to Imam Abu Hanifa's position.
5
Conclude the practical implication
The student must not treat all statements in a matn as equal in authority. When studying a ruling, one should verify whether it is from Zāhir al-Riwāyah or a later derivation, and whether it follows the view of Abu Hanifa or the Sahibayn.
This methodological awareness is critical for proper fiqh research and fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه قد اشتهر أنَّ المتون موضوعةٌ لنقل أصل المذهب ومسائل ظاهر الرواية، وهذا حكم غالبيّ لا كلي، فإنّه كثيراً ما يذكر أرباب المتون مسألة هي من تخريجات المشايخ المتقدمين، مخالفة لمسلكِ الأئمة المتبوعين : كمسألة (العشر في العشر في باب نجاسة الحوض وطهارته)، فإنّها من تحديدات المشايخ المتقدمين، وأصل المذهب خال عن هذا ، كما ستعرفه في موضعِهِ إن شاء الله تعالى. وكذا ما اشتهر أنّ المتون موضوعةٌ لنقل مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة، حكم غالبي لا أكثري ، فكثيراً ما ذكروا فيها مذهب صاحبيه إذا كان راجحاً، كما في بحث (السجدة بالجبهة والأنف) وغيره.
Know that it is well-known that the texts (mutun) are established to transmit the original madhhab and the issues of Zahir al-Riwayah. This is a general rule, not universal. For indeed, often the authors of texts mention an issue that is from the derivations of the later scholars, contrary to the way of the founding imams. Like the issue of 'the ten in the ten' in the chapter of the impurity and purity of the basin, for it is from the determinations of the later scholars, and the original madhhab is free from this, as you will know in its place, God willing. Likewise, what is well-known that the texts are established to transmit the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa is a general rule, not a majority one. For often they mention in them the madhhab of his two companions if it is preponderant, as in the discussion of prostration with the forehead and the nose and other issues.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a methodological clarification from the commentator. He addresses two common assumptions about Hanafi texts (mutun). First, that they only contain the original rulings of the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) from Zahir al-Riwayah. The author corrects this by saying it is a general tendency, not absolute. He gives the example of the issue of 'al-ashr fi al-ashr' (ten in ten) concerning the ruling of an overflowing basin's water—this ruling was actually derived by later scholars, not from the founding imams. Second, that the texts only transmit Abu Hanifa's view; the author notes that often they include the view of the two companions when it is preponderant, as in the ruling that prostration must involve both forehead and nose. This passage teaches the student to understand that the Hanafi school is not monolithic in its textual transmission; later scholarship and tarjih (preferring) of weaker but stronger-dalil views are part of the tradition.

Key Terms
متون (mutūn): The core texts or compendia in the Hanafi school, such as al-Mukhtār, al-Kanz, etc., typically attributed to transmitting the original madhhab.
ظاهر الرواية (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing the primary transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school.
العشر في العشر (al-ʿashr fī al-ʿashr): A specific issue about water used for purification: when a small amount of water (ten spans) is used, it retains some impurity? Actually it refers to measuring the basin: if the water is ten by ten, it is considered not flowing?

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the rule about mutun is 'ghālibī lā kullī' (general, not universal)?
A) Because mutun sometimes contain rulings from later scholars not in the original madhhab
B) Because mutun always contain only Zahir al-Riwayah
C) Because mutun never mention the views of the two companions
D) Because mutun are not used in fatwa

Key Takeaway
Mutun in the Hanafi school are authoritative but not infallible; they may include later rulings and views of the Sahibayn, so they must be used with awareness of their scope.

Prohibition of giving fatwa from certain brief books
Stating a fatwa: it is not permissible to give fatwa from certain abridged works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding fatwa from brief books and identify the two categories of books that are not permissible to use.

Core Idea
A mufti may only issue fatwas from authoritative, comprehensive works, not from abridged texts or books by unknown authors.

This lesson examines a crucial ruling for anyone engaged in ifta. It warns against relying on certain abridged or poorly sourced texts. Understanding this principle safeguards the integrity of fatwa by ensuring that rulings are based on reliable, detailed sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that giving fatwa from certain books is not permissible (lā yajūz), which indicates prohibition (tahrīm).
The act is issuing a legal ruling (fatwa).
2
Identify the two prohibited categories
The first category is brief books (al-kutub al-mukhtasarah), which may omit necessary details. The second is books whose author's reliability is unknown.
Examples are provided for each category.
3
Note the examples
Brief books include al-Nahr, Sharh al-Kanz by al-'Aynī, and al-Durr al-Mukhtar. Unreliable author books include Sharh al-Kanz by Mullā Miskīn and Sharh al-Niqāyah by al-Quhistānī.
These examples help identify which books are considered problematic.
4
Understand the rationale
Brief books lack thoroughness, leading to potential errors. Unknown author reliability risks weak or incorrect transmission, undermining the fatwa's validity.
The rationale is to preserve the accuracy and trustworthiness of fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة الدراسة الرابعة في فوائد متفرقة مفيدة للمفتي والمصنّف قال في «رد المحتار» نقلاً عن «شرح الأشباه» للشيخ هبة الله البَعْلِي)، قال شيخنا العلامة صالح: لا يجوز الإفتاء: ١. من الكتب المختصرة، كـ «النهر» (۳) ، و «شرح الكنز» للعيني)، و«الدر المختار شرح تنویر الأبصار». ٢. أو لعدم الاطلاع على حال مصنفيها ، كـ«شرح الكنز» لملا مسكين)، و«شرح النقاية» للقُهُسْتانِي
Benefit: The Fourth Study: In miscellaneous benefits useful for the mufti and author. He said in Radd al-Muhtār, quoting from Sharh al-Ashbāh by Shaykh Hibatullah al-Ba‘lī: 'Our teacher, the scholar Salih, said: It is not permissible to give fatwa from the brief books, like al-Nahr, and Sharh al-Kanz by al-‘Aynī, and al-Durr al-Mukhtār Sharh Tanwīr al-Absār. Or due to lack of knowledge about the condition of their authors, like Sharh al-Kanz by Mullā Miskīn, and Sharh al-Niqāyah by al-Quhistānī.'
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a practical ruling for muftis and authors (musannifs). It comes from the commentary of al-Haskafi? Actually it's quoting from Radd al-Muhtār. The ruling categorically states that a mufti should not issue fatwas from certain abridged ('mukhtasarah') books. Two reasons are given: first, the books themselves are too brief and may lack nuance; examples: al-Nahr (presumably al-Nahr al-Fā'iq by Ibn Nujaym), Sharh al-Kanz by al-‘Aynī (Badr al-Din al-‘Aynī), and al-Durr al-Mukhtār (the famous text). Second, because the reliability of the author is unknown or questioned; examples: Sharh al-Kanz by Mullā Miskīn (Mu‘īn al-Dīn) and Sharh al-Niqāyah by al-Quhistānī (Shams al-Dīn). The student should understand that not every Hanafi text is suitable for fatwa; only those that are comprehensive and authored by trustworthy scholars with knowledge of the madhhab's foundations.

Key Terms
الإفتاء (al-iftā’): The act of issuing a legal ruling (fatwa) on a matter of Islamic law.
الكتب المختصرة (al-kutub al-mukhtaṣarah): Abridged or concise legal texts that may omit details necessary for accurate fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is too detailed
B) Because the author's reliability is unknown
C) Because it is a commentary on al-Kanz
D) Because it is a primary text

Key Takeaway
A mufti must only issue fatwas from comprehensive, authoritative works, and must avoid abridged texts or those by unknown authors.

Hierarchy of Hanafi Imams for Fatwa
States the order of preference among Hanafi imams when they differ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy of imams to determine which opinion a mufti should follow in case of intra-madhhab disagreement.

Core Idea
A non-mujtahid mufti must follow a fixed hierarchy: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad; a mujtahid may prefer by evidence.

In the Hanafi school, when the founding imams differ, a mufti needs a clear rule to decide which opinion to give as fatwa. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah presents two views: an absolute hierarchy from al-Sirajiyyah, and a choice when Abu Hanifa's two students oppose him. The author resolves the apparent contradiction by distinguishing between a non-mujtahid mufti (who must follow the hierarchy) and a mujtahid (who can weigh evidence).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two views
The first view states an absolute order: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and Hasan. The second view gives the mufti a choice when Abu Hanifa's side opposes his two companions.
Both views are internal to the Hanafi school.
2
Determine the preferred view for a non-mujtahid
The author says the first view is more correct if the mufti is not a mujtahid.
This restricts the second view to those with ijtihad capacity.
3
Reconcile with al-Hawi al-Qudsi
Al-Hawi al-Qudsi says to consider the strength of evidence, but this applies only to those capable of tarjih. Thus, no contradiction.
The reconciliation hinges on the mufti's level of expertise.
4
Apply the hierarchy to a scenario
Given a specific intra-Hanafi dispute, decide which opinion the mufti should follow based on his level.
Practice with hypothetical cases to internalize the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) فوائد متفرقة (٤) إذا اتفق أصحابنا على أمر يفتي به المفتي وإذا اختلفوا فيه : فقيل : الفتوى على الإطلاق على قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، ثم قول أبي يوسف ، ثم قول محمد رحمهما الله، ثم قول زفره والحسن بن زياد . وقيل : إذا كان أبو حنيفة له في جانب وصاحباه في جانب فالمفتي بالخيار، والأول أصح إذا لم يكن المفتي مجتهداً). كذا في «الفتاوى السراجية)، واختار في «الحاوي القدسي » الاعتبار لقوة الدليل، وهذا فيمن له قدرة على الترجيح، فلا مخالفة بينه وبين كلام «السراجية»
(3) Miscellaneous benefits. (4) If our associates (Hanafi scholars) agree on a matter, the mufti gives fatwa accordingly. If they differ: it is said that fatwa is absolutely according to the statement of Abu Hanifa, then the statement of Abu Yusuf, then the statement of Muhammad, then the statement of Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. And it is said: if Abu Hanifa is on one side and his two companions are on the other, the mufti has a choice. The first view is more correct if the mufti is not a mujtahid. This is in al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyyah. And al-Hawi al-Qudsi chose consideration of the strength of evidence, and this is for one who has ability to prefer, so there is no contradiction between it and the statement of al-Sirajiyyah.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a key rule for muftis regarding intra-Hanafi differences. The author presents two views: the first (from al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyyah) gives an absolute hierarchy: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. The second view allows the mufti to choose between Abu Hanifa and his two companions when they are opposed. The author prefers the first view (the hierarchy) for a mufti who is not a mujtahid. However, he reconciles this with al-Hawi al-Qudsi, which considers the strength of evidence, noting that this applies to those capable of preferring (tarjīh). Thus, a non-mujtahid mufti follows the hierarchy; a capable one may prefer based on evidence.

Key Terms
الفتوى على الإطلاق (al-fatwā ʿalā al-iṭlāq): Fatwa is given absolutely according to the stated order without choice
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): Preferring one evidence over another based on strength
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): One who has the capacity to derive rulings from evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what should a non-mujtahid mufti do when Abu Hanifa and his two students differ?
A) He may choose any opinion he wishes
B) He must follow Abu Hanifa absolutely
C) He must follow the majority of scholars
D) He must follow the strongest evidence

Key Takeaway
A non-mujtahid mufti must follow the hierarchy: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad; a mujtahid may choose by evidence.

Fatwa When No Ruling from Early Hanafi Imams
Rules for mufti when early Hanafi imams give no clear answer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three-step methodology for issuing a fatwa when early Hanafi imams have no clear ruling and apply it to a hypothetical scenario.

Core Idea
When early imams are silent, the mufti follows later consensus, then majority, then ijtihad.

When faced with a novel issue not addressed by Abu Hanifa or his immediate students, a Hanafi mufti cannot simply remain silent. This passage from al-Hawi al-Qudsi provides a clear hierarchy for deriving rulings from later scholars (al-mashāyikh al-muta'akhkhirūn). Understanding this process is essential for navigating the Hanafi tradition beyond the core texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the gap
Confirm that no clear answer (jawāb ẓāhir) exists from any of the early Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, etc.). This triggers the need for a supplementary methodology.
The gap must be genuine; if an early imam's statement exists, it is followed first.
2
Check later scholars' consensus
If the later scholars (al-mashāyikh al-muta'akhkhirūn) have a single unanimous statement (qawl wāḥid), it must be adopted. Their authority is binding when early imams are silent.
Later scholars include those from the 4th century onwards.
3
If differing, follow the majority among reliable
If later scholars differ, the mufti follows the position of the majority among those deemed reliable (mu'tamad 'alayhim), such as Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, and Abu al-Layth.
Reliability is key: not all later scholars carry equal weight.
4
If still no answer, perform ijtihad
If even the reliable later scholars have no statement, the mufti must exert ijtihad with careful reflection (ta'ammul, tadabbur, ijtihād) to find a ruling that discharges his responsibility (kharaj 'an al-'uhda).
This ijtihad is within the Hanafi framework, not independent of it.
5
Avoid random fatwa
The mufti must never speak randomly (jazāfan) or without grounding his opinion in the tradition. The entire hierarchy aims to prevent arbitrary rulings.
This is a key adab (etiquette) of ifta.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) وذكر في «الحاوي» أيضاً : «إذا لم يوجد في الحادثة عن واحد من أئمتنا جواب ظاهر، وتكلّم فيه المشايخ المتأخرون قولاً واحداً يؤخذ به، فإن اختلفوا يؤخذ بقول الأكثرين من اعتمد عليه كأبي حفص، وأبي جعفر، وأبي الليث، وغيرهم ممن يعتمد عليه، وإن لم يوجد منهم جواب البتة نصاً ، ينظرُ المفتي فيها نظر تأمل وتدبّر واجتهاد ؛ ليجد فيها ما يقرب إلى الخروج عن العهدة، ولا يتكلم فيها جزافاً». انتهى.
(3) And it is mentioned in al-Hawi as well: 'If an apparent answer is not found in the incident from any of our imams, and the later scholars have spoken about it with a single statement, it is accepted. If they differ, the statement of the majority of those who are relied upon is accepted, such as Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, and others who are relied upon. And if no clear answer is found from them at all, the mufti must look into it with reflection, deliberation, and ijtihad to find what brings him closer to discharging his responsibility, and he should not speak about it randomly.'
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage provides a fatwa methodology when no ruling from the early Hanafi imams (like Abu Hanifa, his students) is available. It comes from al-Hawi al-Qudsi. The ruling: first, look at statements of later scholars (mutā'akhkhirūn). If they agree, follow their consensus. If they differ, follow the majority among reliable later scholars (e.g., Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth). If even they have no statement, the mufti must exert ijtihad with careful reflection to fulfill his duty, avoiding random speech. This shows the Hanafi methodology for expanding the madhhab beyond the founding texts.

Key Terms
المشايخ المتأخرون (al-mashāyikh al-muta'akhkhirūn): Later Hanafi scholars after the founding imams (e.g., from 4th century onwards)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hawi al-Qudsi, what should a mufti do if none of the early Hanafi imams have a clear answer on a new issue?
A) Refuse to give a fatwa
B) Follow the opinion of the earliest available imam
C) First check later scholars' consensus, then majority, then perform ijtihad
D) Follow the caliph's decree

Key Takeaway
When early Hanafi imams have no clear ruling, the mufti follows a three-step hierarchy: later scholars' consensus, majority among reliable later scholars, then ijtihad.

The Mufti's Obligation to Follow the Preponderant Opinion
Quotes from Hanafi authorities on the duties of a mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a pure muqallid and a muqallid with capacity, and state the obligation of following the preponderant opinion in fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must follow the raajih; arbitrary selection is ignorance and violates consensus.

The opening of the passage delivers a strong condemnation: any mufti who picks and chooses opinions without considering which is preponderant is ignorant and has ruptured scholarly consensus. It then defines two categories of muftis – the pure muqallid and the one capable of scrutiny – and assigns distinct duties to each. This lesson unpacks the fundamental rule that a mufti is not free to select any view; he must act on the mu'tamad (relied-upon position) of the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condemned practice
The passage condemns arbitrary selection of opinions without tarjih (weighing). Why is this a violation of consensus?
The text says: 'من يكتفي أن يكون فتواه أو عمله موافقاً لقول أو وجه ... فقد جهل وخرق الإجماع'.
2
Recognize the two types of muftis
The text distinguishes between a 'muqallid mahd' (pure muqallid) and a 'muqallid lahu al-ahliyya li al-nazar' (muqallid with capacity for scrutiny). Identify their definitions.
The pure muqallid lacks ability to weigh evidence; the capable one can perform tarjih but is still bound by corrected positions.
3
State the rule for each type
For the pure muqallid: must follow what the mashayikh have corrected (sahhaha). For the capable muqallid: must act on what he prefers but issue fatwa according to what the mashayikh corrected.
The source says: 'على الأوّل اتباع ما صححه المشايخ، والثاني له الترجيح والتصحيح، وعليه العمل بما رجح عنده، والإفتاء بما صححه المشايخ'.
4
Understand the source authority
Recognize that this ruling comes from later fatwa works (fatawa mutakhkhirin), not the original six books. It is authoritative for today's mufti.
The authority weight is 'fatawa_mutakhkhirin'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدراسة الرابعة: فوائد متفرقة للمفتي
من يكتفي أن يكون فتواه أو عمله موافقاً لقول أو وجه في المسألة، ويعمل بما شاءَ من الأقوال أو الوجوه من غير نظر في الترجيح، فقد جهل وخرق الإجماع.
وفي فتاواه أيضاً في موضع آخر: «الناس بين مقلد محض، ومقلّد له الأهلية للنظر، فعلى الأوّل اتباع ما صححه المشايخ، والثاني له الترجيح والتصحيح، وعليه العمل بما رجح عنده، والإفتاء بما صححه المشايخ؛ لأن السائل إنما يسأله عما هو المذهب عند أهله».
وفي «الدر المختار» أخذاً من «تصحيح القدوري» لقاسم بن قطلوبغا: «إن قلت: قد يحكون أقوالاً بلا ترجيح، وقد يختلفون في الصحيح، قلت: يعمل بمثل ما عملوا به من اعتبار تغيّر العرف وأحوال الناس، وما هو الأرفق، وما ظهر عليه التعامل وما قوي وجهه، ولا يخلو الوجود عمّن يميّز هذا حقيقة لا ظناً، وعلى من لم يميّز أن يرجع لمن يميّز؛ البراءة ذمّته».
وهذا أيضاً من قواعد الفقيه المتفقه في أصول الإفتاء؛ إذ فيه: إذا كان في المسألة قولان أو روايتان أو أكثر وجب الأخذ بما رجحه المجتهدون في المذهب، فإن المسألة التي رجحها هؤلاء يجب على المفتي المقلد اتباعها سواء كان المرجح قولاً للإمام الأعظم أو لأحد من أصحابه، فما رجحه المرجحون مقدّم على كل ما سواه؛ لأن أهل الترجيح مع شدة ورعهم والتزامهم بالمذهب رجّحوا هذا القول لأسباب وضحت لهم من قوة الدليل، ومن ضرورة الناس وتغير الزمان والعرف وغير ذلك فالعمل بترجيحهم أولى. فمثلا: قال ابن قطلوبغا: «ما يصححه قاضي خان مقدّم على تصحيح غيره؛ لأنه فقيه النفس».
وفي «كتاب الرضاع» من «البحر الرائق»: «الفتوى إذا اختلفت كان الترجيح لظاهر الرواية».
وفيه في باب مصرف الزكاة: «إذا اختلف التصحيح وجب الفحص عن ظاهر الرواية والرجوع إليها».
وفيه في «باب قضاء الفوائت»: «إذا اختلف التصحيح والفتوى، فالعمل بما وافق المتون أولى».
وفي «غنية المستملي شرح منية المصلّي» في «بحث التيمم»: «جعل العلماء الفتوى على قول الإمام الأعظم في العبادات مطلقاً، وهو الواقع بالاستقراء ما لم يكن عنه رواية؛ كقول المخالف كما في طهارة الماء المستعمل والتيمم فقط عند عدم غير نبيذ التمر».
وفيه أيضاً في بحث تعديل الأركان: «قد علمت أن مقتضى الدليل في كل من الطمأنينة والقومة والجلسة الوجوب، كذا قاله الشيخ كمال الدين ابن الهمام ولا ينبغي أن يعدل عن الدراية إذا وافقتها رواية».
وفي «الأشباه والنظائر»: «الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف فيما يتعلق بقضاء...»
Fourth Study: Miscellaneous Benefits for the Mufti. Whoever is satisfied that his fatwa or practice agrees with a saying or aspect in the issue, and acts according to whatever saying or aspect he wishes without consideration of preference (tarjih), has become ignorant and violated consensus. And in his Fatawa also in another place: "People are between a pure muqallid, and a muqallid who has the capacity for scrutiny. The first must follow what the mashayikh have corrected (sahhaha). The second has the right of preference and correction, and it is upon him to act according to what he has preferred and to issue fatwa according to what the mashayikh have corrected, because the questioner only asks him about what is the madhhab among its people." And in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, taking from Tashih al-Quduri by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha: "If you say: They may relate sayings without preference, and they may differ regarding what is sahih. I say: One should act like they acted, considering change of custom (urf), conditions of people, what is more convenient (arfaq), what has become prevalent in transactions, and what has a stronger aspect. And existence is not devoid of one who distinguishes this truly, not just speculatively. And he who cannot distinguish should refer to one who can, for the sake of his innocence." This also from the rules of the fiqh student in Usul al-Ifta: If in a matter there are two sayings or two narrations or more, it is obligatory to take what the mujtahids in the madhhab have preferred. So the matter that they have preferred must be followed by the muqallid mufti, whether the preferred is a saying of the Supreme Imam or one of his companions. What the preferrers have preferred is given precedence over all else, because the people of preference, with their extreme piety and commitment to the madhhab, have preferred this saying for reasons that became clear to them from strength of evidence, necessity of people, change of time and custom, etc. So acting on their preference is better. For example, Ibn Qutlubugha said: "What Qadi Khan has corrected is given precedence over the correction of others because he is a jurist of high capability." And in Kitab al-Rada' from al-Bahr al-Raiq: "If fatwas differ, preference is given to the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya)." And in it, in Bab Masraf al-Zakat: "If correction (tashih) differs, it is obligatory to investigate the apparent transmission and refer to it." And in it, in Bab Qada' al-Fawa'it: "If correction and fatwa differ, then acting on what agrees with the texts (mutun) is better." And in Ghunyat al-Mustamli Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, in Bahth al-Tayammum: "The scholars placed the fatwa on the saying of the Supreme Imam in acts of worship absolutely, and that is what has occurred by induction as long as there is no narration from him; like the saying of the opponent as in the purity of used water and tayammum only when there is no date water." And also in Bahh Ta'dil al-Arkan: "You have known that the requirement of the evidence in each of tuma'nina (serenity), qawma (standing), and jalsa (sitting) is obligation (wujub). Thus says Shaykh Kamal al-Din Ibn al-Humam, and it is not proper to turn away from understanding (diraya) when a narration (riwaya) agrees with it." And in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir: "Fatwa is on the saying of Abu Yusuf in matters related to qada..."
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rulings from later Hanafi authorities concerning the methodology of issuing fatwas (ifta). It opens by condemning the practice of arbitrarily selecting any opinion without considering which is preponderant (rajih). Such an act is deemed ignorance and a violation of scholarly consensus. Then it distinguishes two types of muftis: (1) a pure muqallid, who lacks the ability to weigh evidence and must simply follow what the earlier mashayikh have declared sahih (correct), and (2) a muqallid with some capacity for scrutiny, who may perform tarjih (preference) and tashih (correction) based on his own reasoning, but still must base his fatwa on the corrected positions of the school. The text then quotes al-Durr al-Mukhtar, citing Ibn Qutlubugha, which adds that when multiple correct opinions exist, the mufti should consider changes in custom, people's conditions, convenience, prevalent practice, and strength of evidence. If unable to judge, he must refer to someone who can. The passage further cites al-Bahr al-Raiq, stating that preference is given to zahir al-riwaya (the apparent transmissions of Imam Muhammad). It also notes that in matters of worship, the default is to follow Abu Hanifa unless there is a narration from him. Finally, it references al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, indicating that in qada (judicial) matters, Abu Yusuf's opinion is followed. Throughout, the passage emphasizes the obligation of a mufti to adhere to the mu'tamad (relied-upon) position of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjih): Giving preference to one opinion over another based on strength of evidence or other criteria.
تصحيح (tashih): Declaring an opinion as sahih (sound) within the madhhab, often for the purpose of fatwa.
مقلد (muqallid): One who follows another’s ijtihad without independently deriving rulings.
مفتي (mufti): One who issues fatwas, bound by the rules of the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must a pure muqallid (one without capacity for scrutiny) do when issuing a fatwa?
A) Perform his own tarjih based on evidence.
B) Follow whatever opinion he prefers.
C) Follow what the mashayikh have corrected (sahhaha).
D) Refer to the Qur’an and Sunnah directly.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must act on the mu'tamad; personal preference is insufficient.

6 min
Principles for Determining the Mu'tamad: Custom, Zahir al-Riwaya, and Special Cases
Quotes from Hanafi authorities on the duties of a mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the key principles for determining the mu'tamad, including consideration of custom (urf), the priority of zahir al-riwaya, the default in worship (Abu Hanifa), and in judiciary (Abu Yusuf).

Core Idea
When opinions conflict, the mufti must weigh custom, convenience, evidence strength, and adhere to the hierarchy: zahir al-riwaya > others; in worship: Abu Hanifa; in judiciary: Abu Yusuf.

This passage from al-Durr al-Mukhtar and other later works provides concrete criteria for a mufti to determine which opinion to adopt when transmissions differ. It introduces considerations such as change of custom (urf), people's conditions, what is convenient (arfaq), and what has prevalent practice. It also establishes specific rules for different areas: preference for zahir al-riwaya, default to Abu Hanifa in worship, and to Abu Yusuf in judiciary. The lesson explains how a mufti applies these rules systematically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the criteria from al-Durr al-Mukhtar
The text lists: change of custom (taghayyur al-urf), conditions of people (ahwal al-nas), what is more convenient (arfaq), what has become prevalent in transactions (ma zahara alayhi al-ta'amul), and what has a stronger aspect (ma qawiya wajhuhu). These are tools for preferring one opinion over another.
The source says: 'يعمل بمثل ما عملوا به من اعتبار تغيّر العرف وأحوال الناس، وما هو الأرفق، وما ظهر عليه التعامل وما قوي وجهه'.
2
Recognize the hierarchy of transmissions
From al-Bahr al-Raiq: if fatwas differ, preference is given to zahir al-riwaya (the apparent transmission). If correction (tashih) differs, one must investigate and refer to zahir al-riwaya. If correction and fatwa differ, acting on what agrees with the texts (mutun) is better.
The text cites three different rules: preference for zahir al-riwaya in juristic difference; obligation to investigate zahir al-riwaya when tashih differs; and preference for agreement with mutun.
3
Note the special rule in worship
In acts of worship (ibadat), the default is to follow the saying of Abu Hanifa absolutely, as long as there is no narration from him. If there is a narration from him, it is followed. This is by induction (istiqra).
From Ghunyat al-Mustamli: 'جعل العلماء الفتوى على قول الإمام الأعظم في العبادات مطلقاً'.
4
Note the special rule in judiciary
In matters of qada (judiciary), the preferred view is that of Abu Yusuf. This is stated in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir: 'الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف فيما يتعلق بقضاء'.
The text is truncated but the principle is clear: in judicial matters, Abu Yusuf's opinion is given priority.
5
Understand the fallback: refer to experts
If the mufti cannot distinguish the correct view himself, he must refer to someone who can. The passage says: 'وعلى من لم يميّز أن يرجع لمن يميّز؛ البراءة ذمّته'.
This is a duty to safeguard the integrity of the fatwa.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjih): Giving preference to one opinion over another based on strength of evidence or other criteria.
تصحيح (tashih): Declaring an opinion as sahih (sound) within the madhhab, often for the purpose of fatwa.
مقلد (muqallid): One who follows another’s ijtihad without independently deriving rulings.
مفتي (mufti): One who issues fatwas, bound by the rules of the madhhab.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The apparent or clear transmission, referring to the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, which are the most authoritative sources of the Hanafi school.
عرف (urf): Custom or customary practice that is taken into account in legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the general rule for fatwa in matters of worship (ibadat)?
A) Follow the view of Abu Yusuf.
B) Follow the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani.
C) Follow the view of the Supreme Imam (Abu Hanifa) absolutely, unless a narration from him exists.
D) Follow the view that is most convenient for the people.

Key Takeaway
The mufti uses multiple criteria and a hierarchy of sources to determine the mu'tamad, with special rules for worship and judiciary.

The Core Hierarchy of Hanafi Fatwa
Rules for muftis on prioritizing rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchy of Hanafi fatwa: prioritize Zahir al-Riwayah and Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, and identify when necessity allows deviation.

Core Idea
Prefer Zahir al-Riwayah and Imam Abu Hanifa's view except when necessity dictates otherwise.

A mufti must navigate between conflicting rulings within the Hanafi school. This lesson establishes the primary hierarchy: the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) and the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa form the default for fatwa, especially in acts of worship. You will learn when to investigate texts and when deviation is permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of the rule
Pinpoint which classical work (e.g., al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Ghaniat al-Mustamli) states each principle. This helps you trace its authority.
Each quote comes from a respected Hanafi reference.
2
Classify the type of conflict
Determine whether the conflict is between opinions (fatwa), between corrections (tas-hih), or between a narration and evidence.
Different rules apply to each type.
3
Apply the appropriate priority rule
If opinions differ, prefer Zahir al-Riwayah. If correction differs, investigate Zahir al-Riwayah. If fatwa and correction differ, prefer what agrees with established texts.
These are sequential: first check Zahir al-Riwayah, then texts.
4
Check for the worship exception
In acts of worship, Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is absolute unless no narration exists from him; then the opponent's view may be taken (e.g., used water, tayammum).
This is a default, not a rigid rule.
5
Apply the default: Imam al-A'zam
Unless necessity dictates, fatwa and action must follow Imam Abu Hanifa. Deviation is only for necessity.
Necessity is narrowly defined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية

الدراسة الرابعة فوائد متفرقة للمفتي

وفي «كتاب الرضاع» من «البحر الرائق»: «الفتوى إذا اختلفت كان الترجيح لظاهر الرواية». انتهى. وفيه في باب مصرف الزكاة: «إذا اختلف التصحيح وجب الفحص عن ظاهر الرواية والرجوع إليها». انتهى. وفيه في «باب قضاء الفوائت»: «إذا اختلف التصحيح والفتوى، فالعمل بما وافق المتون أولى». انتهى. وفي «غنية المستملي شرح منية المصلي» في «بحث التيمم»: «جعل العلماء الفتوى على قول الإمام الأعظم في العبادات مطلقاً، وهو الواقع بالاستقراء ما لم يكن عنه رواية؛ كقول المخالف كما في طهارة الماء المستعمل والتيمم فقط عند عدم غير نبيذ التمر». انتهى. وفيه أيضاً في بحث تعديل الأركان: «قد علمت أن مقتضى الدليل في كل من الطمأنينة والقومة والجلسة الوجوب، كذا قاله الشيخ كمال الدين ابن الهمام، ولا ينبغي أن يعدل عن الدراية إذا وافقتها رواية». انتهى. وفي «الأشباه والنظائر»: «الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف فيما يتعلق بالقضاء». كما في «القنية» و«البزازية». انتهى. وفي «شرح البيري للأشباه»: «إن الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف أيضاً في الشهادات، وعلى قول زفر في سبع عشرة مسألة حررتها في رسالة». انتهى. وفي باب قضاء الفوائت من «البحر الرائق»: «المسألة إذا لم تذكر في ظاهر الرواية، وثبتت في رواية أخرى تعين المصير إليها». انتهى. وفي «كتاب الوقف» منه: «متى كان في المسألة قولان مصححان جاز القضاء والإفتاء بأحدهما». انتهى. وفي «كتاب الشهادات» من «الفتاوى الخيرية»: «المقرر عندنا أنه لا يفتي ولا يعمل إلا بقول الإمام الأعظم، ولا يعدل عنه إلى قولهما أو قول أحدهما أو قول غيرهما، إلا لضرورة». انتهى.
The mainstay of the care on the commentary of the protection

Fourth study: Miscellaneous benefits for the mufti

And in the 'Book of Breastfeeding' from 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq': 'When rulings differ, preference is given to the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah).' End. And in it, in the chapter on the disbursement of zakat: 'When correction differs, it is obligatory to investigate the apparent transmission and refer to it.' End. And in it, in the chapter on making up missed prayers: 'When correction and fatwa differ, acting according to what agrees with the texts (al-mutun) is preferable.' End. And in 'Ghaniat al-Mustamli Sharh Munyat al-Musalli' in the 'Discussion on Tayammum': 'The scholars have established the fatwa upon the statement of the Greatest Imam [Abu Hanifa] in acts of worship absolutely, and that is what occurs by induction, as long as there is no [contrary] narration from him, like the statement of the opponent as in the purity of used water and tayammum only when there is no date juice.' End. And in it also in the discussion on the adjustment of the pillars: 'You have known that the requirement of the evidence in each of tranquility (tuma'ninah), standing (qawmah), and sitting (jalsah) is obligation. Thus said Shaykh Kamal al-Din Ibn al-Humam, and it is not appropriate to deviate from the reliable source (al-dirayah) when a narration agrees with it.' End. And in 'al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir': 'The fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf concerning matters related to judiciary.' As in 'al-Qunyah' and 'al-Bazzaziyyah'. End. And in 'Sharh al-Biri li al-Ashbah': 'Indeed the fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf also in testimonies, and on the statement of Zufar in seventeen issues which I have compiled in a treatise.' End. And in the chapter on making up missed prayers from 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq': 'When an issue is not mentioned in the apparent transmission but is established in another transmission, it is necessary to adopt it.' End. And in the 'Book of Endowments' from it: 'Whenever there are two valid opinions on an issue, judiciary and fatwa are permissible with either of them.' End. And in the 'Book of Testimonies' from 'al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah': 'The established principle with us is that one does not give fatwa or act except according to the statement of the Greatest Imam, nor does one deviate from it to their [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's] statement, or the statement of one of them, or the statement of others, except out of necessity.' End.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rules for muftis on how to prioritize among conflicting rulings within the Hanafi madhhab. It opens with a general principle from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: when rulings differ, preference is given to Zahir al-Riwayah (the apparent transmission from Imam Muhammad's six core books). In the chapter on zakat, it adds that if corrections (tas-hih) differ, one must investigate and refer to Zahir al-Riwayah. For missed prayers, if both correction and fatwa differ, acting according to the soundest texts (mutun) is preferred. From Ghaniat al-Mustamli, it is stated that scholars consistently base fatwa on Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion in acts of worship, by induction, unless no narration from him exists—then the opposing view may be taken, as in used water and tayammum with date juice. In the discussion on the pillars of prayer, evidence points to obligation (wujub) for tuma'ninah, qawmah, and jalsah, and one should not abandon a reliable source (dirayah) when a narration supports it. From al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, Abu Yusuf's opinion is followed in judicial matters; from its commentary by al-Biri, also in testimonies, while Zufar's view is taken in seventeen specific issues. Another rule: if an issue is absent from Zahir al-Riwayah but found in another transmission, that must be adopted. For endowments, if two opinions are both considered valid (musahhahan), judges and muftis may choose either. Finally, al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah affirms the default rule: no fatwa or action except on Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, with deviation only for necessity.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The apparent/official transmission of the Hanafi school, referring to the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.).
الإمام الأعظم (al-Imam al-A'zam): The Greatest Imam, referring to Abu Hanifa. His opinion is given precedence in acts of worship.
الفتوى (al-fatwa): A legal opinion issued by a qualified jurist (mufti) to a questioner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the default rule for acts of worship?
A) Follow the opinion of Abu Yusuf.
B) Follow the opinion of Imam Muhammad.
C) Follow the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa absolutely, unless no narration from him.
D) Follow the opinion that is easiest.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, always start with Zahir al-Riwayah and Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion; deviate only for necessity.

7 min
Secondary Tarjih: Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and Flexibilities
Specific tarjih rules for judiciary, testimonies, and gaps

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the secondary tarjih rules: when to follow Abu Yusuf (judiciary and testimonies), Zufar (seventeen issues), and when to adopt a ruling absent from Zahir al-Riwayah or choose between two valid opinions.

Core Idea
In judiciary and testimonies follow Abu Yusuf; in 17 specific issues follow Zufar; otherwise, use Zahir al-Riwayah or necessity.

While the general hierarchy prioritizes Zahir al-Riwayah and Imam Abu Hanifa, the school provides specific assignments for certain topics. This lesson covers those exceptions: Abu Yusuf's opinion governs judicial matters and testimonies, Zufar's opinion is taken in seventeen named issues, and cases not found in Zahir al-Riwayah must be resolved from other transmissions. You will also learn when a mufti may choose between two equally valid opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the domain (judiciary, testimonies, or general)
The rule changes based on the chapter. For judiciary (qada) and testimonies (shahadat), Abu Yusuf's opinion is preferred.
Check if the issue is under these chapters.
2
Check for Zufar's seventeen issues
The commentary of al-Biri mentions that Zufar's view is taken in exactly seventeen matters. If the issue is one of them, follow Zufar.
These are compiled in a separate treatise.
3
If not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah
When an issue is absent from the six core books but found in another reliable transmission, that transmission must be adopted.
This prevents gaps in the madhhab.
4
When two opinions are both valid (musahhah)
If both opinions have been declared sound, a judge or mufti may choose either. This provides flexibility.
This applies after the hierarchy has been exhausted.
5
Apply the overall default: Imam Abu Hanifa
Remember from Lesson 1 that outside these specific exceptions, the default remains Imam Abu Hanifa unless necessity dictates otherwise.
These exceptions are limited.

الشهادات (al-shahadat): Testimonies; the law regarding witnesses and evidence.
مصحح (musahhah): An opinion that has been declared valid or sound by later scholars.

D) The mufti should await further clarification.

Know the specific domains: judiciary and testimonies follow Abu Yusuf; Zufar governs 17 issues; and always fill gaps from other transmissions.

Fatwa Methodology: Principles for the Hanafi Mufti
Compilation of fatwa principles from multiple Hanafi sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default fatwa rule, identify exceptions (testimony, 17 issues, Zahir al-Riwayah silence), and apply the principle that an authentic hadith supersedes the madhhab while maintaining Hanafi affiliation.

Core Idea
A mufti follows Imam Abu Hanifa primarily, but an authentic hadith overrides, and exceptions are recognized for necessity or when primary texts are silent.

This passage compiles crucial fatwa rules from key Hanafi sources. It clarifies the mufti's decision-making hierarchy: the default is Imam Abu Hanifa's statement, but necessity (darurah) or the absence of a ruling in the primary narrations (Zahir al-Riwayah) may require adopting another view. Most importantly, it addresses the tension between madhhab authority and authentic hadith: a sahih hadith contrary to the madhhab must be followed, and doing so does not exit one from the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default fatwa principle
From al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya: the mufti must follow Imam Abu Hanifa's statement except for necessity. This is the primary rule.
The passage emphasizes: 'One does not give fatwa nor act except by the statement of the Great Imam.'
2
Recognize exceptions to the default
In testimony matters, the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view; in 17 specific issues, on Zufar's view. Also, if an issue is missing in Zahir al-Riwayah but exists in another narration, that narration must be adopted.
These exceptions show the school's flexibility while maintaining overall structure.
3
Understand the role of Zahir al-Riwayah
Zahir al-Riwayah is the core corpus. If a ruling is not there but is reliably transmitted elsewhere, it becomes binding.
This prevents gaps in the madhhab's guidance.
4
Apply the two sound opinions rule
When two opinions are both considered sound (musahhah), the mufti may choose either for judgement or fatwa.
This grants practical discretion in areas of ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Implement the authentic hadith principle
If a sahih hadith contradicts the madhhab, act on the hadith; it becomes the imam's madhhab. The follower remains Hanafi.
This resolves the apparent conflict between taqlid and sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدراسة الرابعة فوائد متفرقة للمفتي
بالقضاء (1)». كما في «القُنْية»(3) و «البَزَّازيّة» (3) (انتهى)
وفي «شرح البيري للأشباه» () : «إنّ الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف له أيضاً في الشهادات ، وعلى قول زفر له في سبع عشرة مسألة حرَّرتُها في رسالة». انتهى) وفي باب قضاء الفوائت» من «البحر الرائق: رائق»: «المسألة إذا لم تذكر في ظاهر الرواية، وثبتت في رواية أخرى تعين المصير إليها». انتهى () وفي «كتاب الوقف» منه : متى كان في المسألة قولان مصححان جازَ القضاءُ والإفتاء بأحدهما». انتهى. • وفي «كتاب الشهادات» من «الفتاوى الخيرية» (9) : «المقرر عندنا أنه لا يفتي ولا يعمل إلا بقول الإمام الأعظم، ولا يعدل عنه إلى قولهما، أو قول أحدهما، أو غيرهما إلا لضرورة. انتهى
وفي «شرح الأشباه البيري زاده (2) نقلاً عن «شرح الهداية» لابن الشحنة(3) : «إذا صح الحديث وكان على خلافِ المذهب عُمِلَ بالحديث، ويكون ذلك مذهبه، ولا يخرج مقلده عن كونه حنفيّاً بالعمل به ، فقد صح عنه ؛ أي عن الإمام (4)
Fourth study: miscellaneous benefits for the mufti. '...by judgement (1).' As in al-Qunya and al-Bazzaziyya (end). And in Sharh al-Birri on al-Ashbah: 'Indeed the fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf also in the matters of testimony, and on the statement of Zufar in seventeen issues that I have compiled in a treatise.' (end). And in the chapter of 'Making up missed prayers' from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 'If an issue is not mentioned in the Zahir al-Riwaya, and is established in another narration, one must adopt it.' (end). And in 'Kitab al-Waqf' from it: 'Whenever there are two sound opinions on an issue, it is permissible to judge and give fatwa by either.' (end). And in 'Kitab al-Shahadat' from al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya: 'What is established with us is that one does not give fatwa nor act except by the statement of the Great Imam, and one does not deviate from him to their statement (i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), or the statement of one of them, or others except for necessity.' (end). And in Sharh al-Ashbah by al-Birri Zade, quoting from Sharh al-Hidaya by Ibn al-Shihnah: 'If a hadith is authentic and is contrary to the madhhab, the hadith is acted upon, and that becomes his madhhab, and his muqallid does not cease being a Hanafi by acting upon it, for it is authentically reported from him; i.e., from the Imam.'
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of fatwa principles gathered from various authoritative Hanafi sources. It begins by citing a ruling from al-Qunya and al-Bazzaziyya about giving judgement (possibly in a specific context). The text then from Sharh al-Birri on al-Ashbah explains that in matters of testimony (shahadat), the fatwa should follow Abu Yusuf, while in seventeen specific issues, it should follow Zufar. This indicates that while Imam Abu Hanifa's view is primary, there are recognized exceptions where the school defers to his students. Next, from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, it states that if a ruling is not found in the Zahir al-Riwaya (the core transmitted rulings) but is established in another narration, it must be adopted. This principle guides the mufti when the madhhab's primary texts are silent. From the same book's chapter on waqf, it notes that when two opinions are both considered sound (musahhah) by later scholars, it is permissible to judge or give fatwa by either—showing flexibility. Finally, quoting al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya, the general rule is reiterated: the mufti should only act upon Imam Abu Hanifa's statement and should not deviate to Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, or others except under necessity. This emphasizes the authority of the founding Imam. The last quote from Sharh al-Ashbah by al-Birri Zade, quoting Ibn al-Shihnah's Sharh al-Hidaya, addresses a crucial point: if an authentic hadith contradicts the madhhab, the hadith must be followed, and that becomes the madhhab of the imam (as if he would have adopted it if he knew it). The muqallid (follower) does not cease being a Hanafi by acting on such a hadith. This principle allows for correction based on authentic sunnah while maintaining adherence to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The core transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in the six books (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.)
فتوى (fatwa): A non-binding legal opinion issued by a qualified jurist
مقلد (muqallid): A person who follows a madhhab without independent investigation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the default position regarding giving fatwa?
A) Follow Imam Abu Hanifa only, except for necessity
B) Follow Abu Yusuf in all matters
C) Follow Zufar in all matters
D) Choose the easiest opinion

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufti must balance adherence to Imam Abu Hanifa with the imperative to follow authentic hadith, recognizing established exceptions and the binding authority of Zahir al-Riwayah.
